  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d8a85a79-7212-4fc1-9e81-461627af1cb4'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer14128129683836875008"><b>From the <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of <i>The Giver of Stars</i>, discover the love story that captured over 20 million hearts in <i>Me Before You</i>, <i>After You</i>, and <i>Still Me</i>.<b><br/><br/><i>“You’re going to feel uncomfortable in your new world for a bit. But I hope you feel a bit exhilarated too. Live boldly. Push yourself. Don’t settle. Just live well. Just live. Love, Will.”</i><br/> <br/>How do you move </b></b></span>
  <span id="freeText14128129683836875008" style="display:none"><b>From the <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of <i>The Giver of Stars</i>, discover the love story that captured over 20 million hearts in <i>Me Before You</i>, <i>After You</i>, and <i>Still Me</i>.<b><br /><br /><i>“You’re going to feel uncomfortable in your new world for a bit. But I hope you feel a bit exhilarated too. Live boldly. Push yourself. Don’t settle. Just live well. Just live. Love, Will.”</i><br /> <br />How do you move on after losing the person you loved? How do you build a life worth living?<br /> <br />Louisa Clark is no longer just an ordinary girl living an ordinary life. After the transformative six months spent with Will Traynor, she is struggling without him. When an extraordinary accident forces Lou to return home to her family, she can’t help but feel she’s right back where she started.<br /> <br />Her body heals, but Lou herself knows that she needs to be kick-started back to life. Which is how she ends up in a church basement with the members of the Moving On support group, who share insights, laughter, frustrations, and terrible cookies. They will also lead her to the strong, capable Sam Fielding—the paramedic, whose business is life and death, and the one man who might be able to understand her. Then a figure from Will’s past appears and hijacks all her plans, propelling her into a very different future. . . .<br /> <br />For Lou Clark, life after Will Traynor means learning to fall in love again, with all the risks that brings. But here Jojo Moyes gives us two families, as real as our own, whose joys and sorrows will touch you deeply, and where both changes and surprises await.</b></b></span>

<a href="/questions/495858-does-anyone-else-feel-like-a-sequel-is">Does anyone else feel like a sequel is just WRONG? I mean, after the devastating ending of the first book- the whole story was based on the relationship and love between Will and Lou and to try to continue the story without him????? I am completely overwhelmed with emotions.</a>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I think I have a more unpopular opinion in regards to this. Me Before You made me sad...in no way did I feel relieved or find a super positive outlook<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I think I have a more unpopular opinion in regards to this. Me Before You made me sad...in no way did I feel relieved or find a super positive outlook on the book, and I still don't feel Will made the right choice in the end. I NEED to live in a story where Lou moves on and potentially finds happiness. If I were her, I'd have a very hard time letting myself feel vulnerable again.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Lou Clark and Will had me crying and laughing for the few days I encountered them. They became real than people I see on a daily basis. That was a ver<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Lou Clark and Will had me crying and laughing for the few days I encountered them. They became real than people I see on a daily basis. That was a very good novel. I missed them as well when I finished and I cried so bad, snort and everything as I read the chapter when Will says his good byes to Lou. Wow Jojo Moyes outdid herself. I actually do not want to think of a sequel as I am still grieving. You know that grief you have after a good read. I don't think anything should surpass that for this week lol <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_1301650955" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1301650955" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1301650955?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780698411418" href="/book/show/25020381-after-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1301650955" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1119855206423536160">2 1/2 stars. It's hard to have to say this, but it's not completely unexpected either. When I finally gave in to the hype and read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You' title='Me Before You by Jojo Moyes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Me Before You</a> a couple years ago, I absolutely and unapologetically loved it. Like many of its fans, I've been waiting with bated breath for this sequel. <b>But it just isn't strong enough or... needed</b>.<br/><br/>That's what it comes down to. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25020381.After_You__Me_Before_You___2_' title='After You (Me Before You, #2) by Jojo Moyes' rel='nofollow noopener'>After You</a> was written to satisfy a craving in the minds of Lou and Will's fans. When we've loved a book, we all have those questions: what w</span>
  <span id="freeText1119855206423536160" style="display:none">2 1/2 stars. It's hard to have to say this, but it's not completely unexpected either. When I finally gave in to the hype and read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You" title="Me Before You by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a> a couple years ago, I absolutely and unapologetically loved it. Like many of its fans, I've been waiting with bated breath for this sequel. <b>But it just isn't strong enough or... needed</b>.<br /><br />That's what it comes down to. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25020381.After_You__Me_Before_You___2_" title="After You (Me Before You, #2) by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">After You</a> was written to satisfy a craving in the minds of Lou and Will's fans. When we've loved a book, we all have those questions: what will the characters do now? What comes next? But these are natural questions following all loved books. It does not necessarily mean a book should be written to answer those questions. (<i>Cinderella II: Dreams Come True</i>, anyone?)<br /><br />The result of Moyes trying to create a new episode of the story out of such questions is <b>a book that feels like fanfiction, not a worthy sequel</b>.<br /><br />This book attempts to tie up all loose ends in Lou's life. It's quite enjoyable because Lou is as comical and lovable as we remember, but a certain humourous spark has disappeared now that we don't have the wonderful Lou/Will dynamic. Despite the lingering sadness of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You" title="Me Before You by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a>, I didn't find it to be a depressing book. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25020381.After_You__Me_Before_You___2_" title="After You (Me Before You, #2) by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">After You</a>, on the other hand, is much more depressing for the most part - a fact that does not add depth to it.<br /><br />There's just not that much story to the book, except for the contrived "surprise from Will's past" showing up, and that just turned the book into <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4271.About_a_Boy" title="About a Boy by Nick Hornby" rel="nofollow noopener">About a Boy</a> with female characters - lonely woman in her thirties gains new purpose from helping a problem kid. <br /><br />The new love interest is a nice guy, but is forgettable and I never felt much chemistry between them. Also, I tried really hard to sympathize, <b>but I just despised the selfish, bratty Lily</b>.<br /><br />Everything in this book feels unnatural - created by the author to extend a story that had already been told to its full potential. The various subplots feel like extra padding and seem pointless. What was all that about Lou's mother discovering feminism and refusing to shave her legs? Aside from the cringy portrayal of feminism, why is that even in there?<br /><br />I understand why fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You" title="Me Before You by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a> will feel the need to read this book, but I just don't think it's necessary. It's mildly entertaining at times, but nothing valuable has been added here.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/bookgeekreviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1119855206423536160" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1212513624" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1212513624" />
    <a title="Kristie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13798293-kristie"><img alt="Kristie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595643917p2/13798293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1212513624?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristie" href="/user/show/13798293-kristie">Kristie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525426592" href="/book/show/24941288-after-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13798293-kristie?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13798293-kristie?shelf=gcac_2016">gcac_2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1212513624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11873507693996871665">***If you have not read Me Before You, please note that there are spoilers for the end of that book in this review. ***<br/><br/>I have seen a lot of negative reviews for this book, most of which compare it to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You__Me_Before_You___1_' title='Me Before You (Me Before You, #1) by Jojo Moyes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Me Before You</a>. I get it. Me Before You was amazing. I fell in love with the characters too. This book, however, is not Me Before You. <br/><br/>So many people loved Lou from Me Before You and wanted to know what happened to her after the book ended. Then, when they are given a book that tells them what happen</span>
  <span id="freeText11873507693996871665" style="display:none">***If you have not read Me Before You, please note that there are spoilers for the end of that book in this review. ***<br /><br />I have seen a lot of negative reviews for this book, most of which compare it to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You__Me_Before_You___1_" title="Me Before You (Me Before You, #1) by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a>. I get it. Me Before You was amazing. I fell in love with the characters too. This book, however, is not Me Before You. <br /><br />So many people loved Lou from Me Before You and wanted to know what happened to her after the book ended. Then, when they are given a book that tells them what happened, they automatically compare it to the first one that they loved and realize that it falls short. These people are disappointed in the story because they expect the greatness of Me Before You to continue. Well... I think you need to enter this story knowing that a book that you fall that deeply in love with is a rare thing and it is unlikely that a follow up story will evoke the same emotions. (Please know that, yes, I realize that this does not apply to <i>everyone</i>. Some people will simply not like the story. I am only referring to a specific group of people here...you know who you are.)<br /><br />This book is no exception. It did not evoke in me what Me Before You did. However, it was a good story on its own. If not comparing the two and only looking at After You for its own merits, it is a good story. Maybe it was more about other characters than you had hoped? I enjoyed meeting new characters and watching Lou's life expand. <br /><br />I thought this story was very well done. It showed Lou's struggle with moving on after Will's death. It showed how his death affected other characters and how people struggled to relate following such a tragedy. I still love Lou's character and there are other character's in this book that I really enjoyed - Sam, Donna, Jake... I didn't love Lily, but she grew on me later in the book. I enjoyed the characters in Lou's group and their interactions. Mostly, I enjoyed seeing Lou's struggle, how she was stuck, and how she grew. <br /><br />Overall, I really enjoyed this story and think it is worth a read. Please know if you intend to read it that this is not Lou and Will's story. This is Lou's story of growth and Lily's story of growth, as both learn how to move on from their pasts. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>Thank you to NetGalley and the publisher for providing me with a free electronic copy of this book in exchange for an honest review.</b>
</i> <br /><br /><br />Original Review: <br />Part of me is very excited that this sequel is being written, because I really love Me Before You. However, part of me is really concerned that this sequel is being written, because I love Me Before You. That story had a definite beginning, middle, and end. I really hope this story doesn't spoil that one some how. Oh, how I hope I love it</span>
  <a data-text-id="11873507693996871665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1371794638" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1371794638" />
    <a title="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys"><img alt="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463498958p2/1053760.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1371794638?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" href="/user/show/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys">Shelby *trains flying monkeys*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525426592" href="/book/show/24941288-after-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1371794638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1874819068074618916">When I first heard that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You__Me_Before_You___1_' title='Me Before You (Me Before You, #1) by Jojo Moyes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Me Before You</a> would have a sequel I wondered how Jojo Moyes would be able to pull it off. It either could go fairly decently or be a big old hot mess. <br/>How do you top a book that was perfection to me?<br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448381526i/17132336.jpg' alt='Palm Springs commercial photography' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>The author does have a bit at the beginning asking readers to not spoil anything for other readers and I will respect that, because just because a book doesn't work for me doesn't mean that everyone will feel that same way.<br/>It's just that....I felt so personally invested in</span>
  <span id="freeText1874819068074618916" style="display:none">When I first heard that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You__Me_Before_You___1_" title="Me Before You (Me Before You, #1) by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a> would have a sequel I wondered how Jojo Moyes would be able to pull it off. It either could go fairly decently or be a big old hot mess. <br>How do you top a book that was perfection to me?<br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448381526i/17132336.jpg" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The author does have a bit at the beginning asking readers to not spoil anything for other readers and I will respect that, because just because a book doesn't work for me doesn't mean that everyone will feel that same way.<br>It's just that....I felt so personally invested in that first book. <br>When this one started out I was okay. Lou was battling her grief over Will's death. I know how hard losing someone can be. It's devastating. Hell, Will was a book character and I shed a whole lot of tears over him myself. <br>I feel like JoJo Moyes should have had a best friend that just stopped her when she presented the idea of this book to her. Instead of encouraging her....<br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448381526ra/17132337.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Because, it did not work. AT ALL. <br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448381526ra/17132338.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>Booksource: Netgalley in exchange for review. </i><br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448381526i/17132339.jpg" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>My friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1212106022?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Magdalena</a> did enjoy this book. She writes an amazing review at the link provided. I think it's just up to the individual reader on this one. </span>

<div id="review_1398718250" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1398718250" />
    <a title="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time"><img alt="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365526640p2/13070326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1398718250?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" href="/user/show/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time">Heather K (dentist in my spare time)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780698152045" href="/book/show/25026542-after-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=read-to-review-arc">read-to-review-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=net-galley">net-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=m-f">m-f</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=chick-lit-women-s-fiction">chick-lit-women-s-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=full-of-angst">full-of-angst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=little-to-no-sex-content">little-to-no-sex-content</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1398718250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18265374637535299361">I hate to upset fans of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You' title='Me Before You by Jojo Moyes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Me Before You</a> (hell, I'm a huge fan of <i>Me Before You</i>), but this was a very underwhelming sequel. <b>I think if you are expecting the emotional punch of the first book you are going to be sorely disappointed.</b><br/><br/>I'm not ashamed to say that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You' title='Me Before You by Jojo Moyes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Me Before You</a> had me up reading until very late at night and then crying my eyes out until very early the next morning. It was the kind of book that sticks with you, the kind of book that is extremely hard to follow up. It ended on a very power</span>
  <span id="freeText18265374637535299361" style="display:none">I hate to upset fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You" title="Me Before You by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a> (hell, I'm a huge fan of <i>Me Before You</i>), but this was a very underwhelming sequel. <b>I think if you are expecting the emotional punch of the first book you are going to be sorely disappointed.</b><br /><br />I'm not ashamed to say that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You" title="Me Before You by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a> had me up reading until very late at night and then crying my eyes out until very early the next morning. It was the kind of book that sticks with you, the kind of book that is extremely hard to follow up. It ended on a very powerful note, so any book that calls itself a "sequel" has to match that kind of power. This didn't, not even close. <br /><br />We follow Lou's life a year and a half after the death of Will, and we see what her life has become. Honestly, I didn't enjoy this Lou very much. Gone is any spark, any vitality, any humor, and without those aspects of her personality I had trouble staying engaged with her. I didn't like this pushover Lou, and I barely recognized her from the previous book.<br /> <br />Her life is wholly depressing. <b>Lou is stuck completely in this sort of limbo, and reading about her mostly boring day to day things felt one-note and tedious.</b> Lou's family details, like her mother's newfound feminism and her sister's meddling, seemed contrived and almost silly. I didn't get what those side plots added to the story, and I didn't find them compelling. <br /><br />Lou's love interest was just... there. He was sexy in a classic romance way- the patient, motorcycle-riding savior- but I simply didn't feel the chemistry between him and Lou. <b>It felt like a relationship without weight, certainly without the intensity of Lou's relationship with Will.</b> If you are going to present a love interest to follow the one from Me Before You, it would have to be absolutely epic... this wasn't. <br /><br />And don't get me started on Lily. No spoilers from me, but Lily just irritated me to no end. She was SO selfish, and I struggled to feel much sympathy for her rich-girl plight. I know the author tried to give us reasons to empathize with Lily, especially near the end with her convoluted backstory, but I was rooting for Lou to branch out and have more of the story-line to herself. <br /><br />However, <b>this book's greatest crime, IMO, was that it was boring.</b> I kept putting this book down and starting other stories, only to force myself back to this one after a few hours. And though this book has brief moments of greatness, and it wasn't bad or offensive in any way, it also failed to grab me the way I was expecting it to. After the way <i>Me Before You</i> gripped me, I think this was the biggest let down of all.<br /><br />**Copy provided by the publisher in exchange for an honest review**<br /> <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18265374637535299361" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2060177630" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2060177630" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2060177630?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9781405909075" href="/book/show/29613508-after-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2060177630" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5273810299728217931"><i>”Sometimes I felt as if we were all wading around in grief, reluctant to admit to others how far we were waving or drowning.”</i><br/><br/>Okay, before I start this review I have to admit three things:<br/><br/>1.)	<b>“After You”</b> wasn’t what I expected it to be and headed into a completely different direction than I assumed.<br/>2.)	I think Jojo Moyes was very brave to go into this kind of direction and I appreciate her realistic approach.<br/>3.)	This might turn out to be a rather personal and subjective review. <br/><br/>I know it would be</span>
  <span id="freeText5273810299728217931" style="display:none"><i>”Sometimes I felt as if we were all wading around in grief, reluctant to admit to others how far we were waving or drowning.”</i><br /><br />Okay, before I start this review I have to admit three things:<br /><br />1.)	<b>“After You”</b> wasn’t what I expected it to be and headed into a completely different direction than I assumed.<br />2.)	I think Jojo Moyes was very brave to go into this kind of direction and I appreciate her realistic approach.<br />3.)	This might turn out to be a rather personal and subjective review. <br /><br />I know it would be easy to say that I didn’t like Louisa in this book and a lot of reviewers before me actually did. They said they didn’t like how much she changed, that the happy girl was gone, that she wasted the gift Will had given her, that she was merely existing and not living her dream. Not doing, what Will wanted her to do before he died.<br /><br /><i>“Live boldly. Push yourself. Don’t settle. Just live well. Just live.”</i><br /><br />But what a lot of readers didn’t get – and I'm glad they didn't seem to get it because I’m speaking from personal experience here and I truly wish no one to make an experience like that– is that she was grieving. Yes, Will’s death didn’t come unexpected. It was planned, they all knew it would happen but that didn’t change anything about the fact that she loved him and that he still decided to go. I wasn’t surprised that Lou is a mess at the beginning of this book, I wasn’t surprised, that she didn’t see the world like she planned to, that she didn’t live her dream. Because honestly: How could she? The person she loved, her first and one true love was dead and there was nothing she could have done to stop him, nothing that would have changed his mind.<br /><br /><i>”How could I explain to this girl what Will and I had been to each other, the way I felt that no person in the world had ever understood me like he did or ever would again? How could she understand that losing him was like having a hole shot straight through me, a painful, constant reminder, an absence I could never fill?”</i><br /><br />To lose the person you love? It changes you, it alters your perception, it makes you realize how short life is, it forces you to acknowledge that you won’t live forever, that everything could be over in nothing but a second. You know that you should move on, because life moves on regardless if you want it to or not. If there’s one thing death teaches you, then it’s that life is merciless and doesn’t pause for the living!<br /><br /><i>”So what was the hardest part?” Mr Gopnik said.<br />“I’m sorry?”<br />“Of working for William Traynor. It sounds like quite a challenge.”<br />I hesitated. The room was suddenly very quiet. “Letting him go.” I said. And found myself unexpectedly biting back tears.</i><br /><br />So, yes Louisa is a mess! She’s still so very young and innocent and has to deal with the loss of the man who stole her heart. Of course this experience changed her, of course she isn’t the same person she was before and yes, she is fighting depression! But she is doing everything she can in order to deal with his loss and that’s admirable and needs to be acknowledged.<br /><br />I know a lot of readers might have wanted the book to go in another direction and truth be told I wanted to see a happy Louisa too, but that’s not how things work, that’s not how mourning works. That would have been unrealistic and it would have devalued the love Lou felt for Will. So, is this book an intermediate phase? Yes, it is! But it is necessary! Lou has to grieve in order to be able to move on and to heal and she ultimately does! Boy, how she does! <br /><br />It might have been sad to read her journey, it might have been depressing but it was realistic and wholesome and I can’t thank Jojo Moyes enough for this kind of representation! Because that’s what happens when you lose the person you love! You try to get back on your feet, you try to live on, you fight to be able to enjoy your life! You learn how to cope with your loss, to turn it into something positive! There are days you take one step forward and two steps back, but you learn to be thankful for the fact that you’re still alive! That life is still ahead of you! That the time you spent with your loved one - no matter how long or short lived it might have been - was precious and a gift! And eventually… well eventually you accept your loss and you move on. You finally live the life you know your loved one wanted you to live all along. <br /><br />I could write about Lou’s love interest or the rather unexpected twist that happens right at the beginning of the story. I could write about Lou’s funny family and all their antics, but I think I’ll just leave it at that. <br /><br />For me <b>“After You”</b> is a book about grief and healing. About learning how to live with your scars and about accepting them as a part of you. The loss of a loved one might push you into the abyss but it’s up to you if you fight and crawl out of them or stay there and get lost. It’s a fight no one can help you with, a fight you have to battle on your own. But let me tell you this, it’s a battle that’s always worth it. ;-)<br /><br />So thank you Jojo Moyes, for tackling such a sensitive and serious topic with genuine humour and tentative prudence. Thank you for giving us hope. I can only speak for myself here, but my teenage me really would have needed and appreciated your book! It might be too late for me, but I’m sure many other people will find comfort in your words! <br />And sometimes, well sometimes that’s already enough. =)<br /><br />___________________________________<br /><br />It <b>
  <u>only</u>
</b> took me about five years to get over the first book but I’m very optimistic that I’ll be able to read book two without <s>suffering another severe trauma</s> crying my soul out. <br /><br />I mean it’s got to get better, right? <br />Lou will get happy in this one, she has to! <br /><br />If not I might just end up throwing another book against a wall. &gt;_&lt;<br />Urgh, the heartbreak from “Me Before You” still feels so fresh… and this after five freaking years.<br /><br />I’m going to read this but can anyone hug me when it gets too much? *makes huge puppy eyes*<br />Wish me luck, guys! I get the feeling I might need it. T_T</span>
  <a data-text-id="5273810299728217931" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1691653514" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1691653514" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1691653514?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25041504-after-you">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1691653514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4812088716043875101"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I really, <i>really</i> didn't like ME BEFORE YOU.<br/><br/>It was heartbreaking, but it was the heartbreak of an impartial observer. I liked Louisa Clark, but, for whatever reason, I never connected with her the way I do in a well-developed story, and the story itself was so . . . unlikely. <br/><br/>I suppose it felt like tragedy for tragedy's sake.<br/><br/>And that shit pisses me off. <br/><br/>If you're going to ground my heart into the pavement, there had better be a damn good reason for it.<br/><br/>But ME BEFORE YOU was like Moyes tho</span>
  <span id="freeText4812088716043875101" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br />I really, <i>really</i> didn't like ME BEFORE YOU.<br /><br />It was heartbreaking, but it was the heartbreak of an impartial observer. I liked Louisa Clark, but, for whatever reason, I never connected with her the way I do in a well-developed story, and the story itself was so . . . unlikely. <br /><br />I suppose it felt like tragedy for tragedy's sake.<br /><br />And that shit pisses me off. <br /><br />If you're going to ground my heart into the pavement, there had better be a damn good reason for it.<br /><br />But ME BEFORE YOU was like Moyes thought to herself:<br /><br />1. What's the most impossible falling-in-love scenario I can come up with? Excellent, let's do that.<br />2. How can I make moving the relationship forward equally impossible? *is gleeful* Let's do that, too.<br />3. And how can I make the whole thing pointless, from start to finish, while inflicting the most emotional damage? Wheeeeee! Best! Plan! Everrrrrrr!<br /><br />And look at the title: ME BEFORE YOU. <br /><br />It's deceptively selfish. It's meant to be a love story, right? So it <i>should</i> be YOU BEFORE ME. But the eye glances over it, and the brain makes excuses, so that you don't realize until it's too late that it's a one-sided love story.<br /><br />Or maybe it's ambiguous, and my interpretation is a reflection of my overall experience. <br /><br /><i>Whatever.</i> *kicks aluminum can*<br /><br />The point is that I didn't read AFTER YOU b/c I loved the previous book. I read it b/c I couldn't stomach abandoning Lou under the circumstances ME BEFORE YOU ended on.<br /><br />I saw the same spark Will had seen in Louisa, the unrealized potential, and I decided to give Moyes the chance to cultivate that potential.<br /><br />I. Am. SO. Glad.<br /><br />There's a subtlety to AFTER YOU that was missing in ME BEFORE YOU. It allowed Moyes to craft something entirely different, something that felt <i>real</i>, even after the meticulously crafted WOE of what came before.<br /><br />Louisa Clark transformed from a cardboard placeholder into a person of flesh and blood. Treena, previously, a stock baby sister, spoiled and selfish, became a bright young woman struggling with the consequences of a teenage pregnancy. I could feel her despair and guilt wrestling with her love of the son that had complicated her life. Her parents were equally changed, as were Will's. <br /><br />Then there were the new characters, like the members of Lou's weekly group therapy meeting, who we spent little time with, but who were all clear, individual personalities. <br /><br />And Lily . . . ye gods. That girl broke my heart worse than Will Traynor ever did.<br /><br />But this time I laughed as much as I cried. At the meandering tangents poor Marc (unsuccessfully) tried to rein in during the Moving On Circle meetings. At Thom's boyish antics, the looks exchanged between sisters, Mrs. Clark's refusal to shave her legs after taking a night class of the feminist variety, and a dozen other things besides. <br /><br />And that laughter made the pain bearable, the pain of truths that were ruthless in their simplicity. A child who knew that her mother loved her, but not as much as she loved herself. A group of strangers bound together by grief the rest of the world had forgotten:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I think people get bored of grief,” said Natasha. “It’s like you’re allowed some unspoken allotted time—six months maybe—and then they get faintly irritated that you’re not ‘better.'"</i>
</blockquote><br />The loneliness of a young women trying her best 'to live,' but lacking the heart to do it properly:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Without someone to talk to, every sight I saw—whether it was the Trevi Fountain or a canal in Amsterdam—felt simply like a name on a list that I needed to check off.</i>
</blockquote><br />These were smaller pains, but they were no less potent. They were familiar hurts, relatable, unlike the crafted pain of ME BEFORE YOU. <br /><br />I've always internally scoffed when I've heard or read about someone not realizing they were crying until their face was too wet to ignore, or some Good Samaritan gave them a tissue--how can you cry and not know it? <br /><br />But AFTER YOU taught me that there are some hurts that sneak up on you, that are subconsciously recognized, even when experiencing them vicariously, and <i>several</i> times throughout the reading I found myself similarly effected as those I'd previously ridiculed.<br /><br />Then Treena would give Lou a look that I've received many times from my own sisters:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>She pulled the kind of face at me that told me simultaneously that I was an eejit, and also that this was no surprise to her whatsoever.</i>
</blockquote><br />And I'd be snorting those tears up my nose, b/c laughing.<br /><br />I've seen in several reviews that some readers were disappointed with AFTER YOU, that it didn't deliver the same emotional kidney punch. I'm not going to argue that point, b/c I agree. Instead of the manufactured grief that resulted from a series of events so horrifying that you couldn't help but react to them, regardless of how foreign that grief is to your own life experience, you get the pain from the aftermath of that loss. <br /><br />It's a real pain that few of us aren't familiar with, and that made me feel it all the more deeply.<br /><br />But it was the <i>potential</i> that made the real difference. The potential for something <i>more</i> than unremitting pain. <br /><br />SO. My recommendation is this:<br /><br />1. If you rely on the author to create an emotional response that you're incapable of drudging up on your own, skip AFTER YOU. You'll only be disappointed.<br /><br />2. If you independently FEEL all the things, and don't mind a bit of turmoil on the path to a happy ending, read AFTER YOU immediately. <br /><br />It is lovely. <br /><br />And frustrating, and heartbreaking, and REAL.<br /><br />And in my humble opinion, that makes AFTER YOU an infinitely better story.<br /><br /><b>My review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1551344226" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4812088716043875101" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17002107927909753929"><b>After You (Me Before You, #2), Jojo Moyes</b><br/><br/>After You is a romance novel written by Jojo Moyes, a sequel to Me Before You. The book was first published on 29 September 2015 in the United Kingdom. A second sequel, Still Me, was published in January 2018. <br/><br/>It continues the story of Louisa Clark after Will's death. She is trying to move on. She was convinced by his motivation to change, so she moved to London and got a job in an airport coffee shop. One night, she decides to go up the roof of her build</span>
  <span id="freeText17002107927909753929" style="display:none"><b>After You (Me Before You, #2), Jojo Moyes</b><br /><br />After You is a romance novel written by Jojo Moyes, a sequel to Me Before You. The book was first published on 29 September 2015 in the United Kingdom. A second sequel, Still Me, was published in January 2018. <br /><br />It continues the story of Louisa Clark after Will's death. She is trying to move on. She was convinced by his motivation to change, so she moved to London and got a job in an airport coffee shop. One night, she decides to go up the roof of her building to sit alone when someone from behind her talks to her. She panics and falls off the roof. <br /><br />She breaks many bones and takes a lot of time to heal. After she gets well she enrolls in a moving on circle in a church and lies to everyone and tells them Will's name was Bill. <br /><br />Lily, Will's daughter gets in contact with her and she wants to know everything about her deceased father, who she didn't know existed until he passed away. Lily wants to get to know her grandparents, so she moves in with Louisa. <br /><br />She hates living with her mother, stepfather, and her half-brothers. Meanwhile, Louisa gets to know Sam, the father of one of the boys in her moving on circle. <br /><br />Sam is also one of the ambulance drivers that helped save her life. As she gets to know him, a new love story begins to grow in her life. <br /><br />Nathan gets in contact with her and offers her a job in the USA. She interviews for this job and gets accepted. It is such a hard decision for Lou as she had just started to fall for Sam.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز هفدهم ماه نوامبر سال 2016میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: پس از تو؛ نویسنده: جوجو مویس (مویز)؛ مترجم: مریم فتاحی؛ تهران، آموت، 1394؛ در 560ص؛ شابک 9786003840188؛ موضوع داستانهای نویسندگان انگلیسی - سده 21م<br /><br />راوی ادامه ی رمان «من پیش از تو»؛ با عنوان «پس از تو»؛ دختری جوان به نام «لوسیا (لو) (لوئیزا) کلارک» است، دختر پرستاری که دربهای دنیای بزرگتری، به رویش گشوده شده؛ تا او با عبور از آنها، زندگی را از سر بگیرد، و آهنگی دیگر از بودنِ خویش بنوازد؛ «لوسیا» با تجربه ی تازه ای روبرو می‌شود، و او یکبار دیگر در آزمون زندگی شرکت می‌کند، و باز بر سر دوراهی می‌ایستد، و در نهایت مجبور می‌شود انتخابش را و بزرگترین تصمیم برای زندگی‌ خویش را بگیرد...؛<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 14/07/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14191362148207497838">It’s very rare that I love the second book, in a series, as much as the first. Yet, here I am, handing out five well deserved stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️!!!   <span id="freeText14191362148207497838" style="display:none">It’s very rare that I love the second book, in a series, as much as the first. <div id="review_1894484137" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1894484137" />
    <a title="Alejandro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro"><img alt="Alejandro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328672389p2/665584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1894484137?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alejandro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alejandro" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro">Alejandro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=novel">novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1894484137" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6276919956823340697"><b>
  <u>Louisa Clark returns!!!</u>
</b><br/><br/><br/><i>This novel is the sequel to “Me Before You”, so you need to read that book first to be able to engage into this one.</i><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>BECAUSE LIFE DOESN’T END LIKE BOOKS</u>
</b><br/><br/>I am truly glad that Jojo Moyes, the author, decided to write this sequel, since while <i>Me Before You</i> has a proper closure and you could be totally satisfied there, well, life doesn’t have “endings” like the books, and certainly while Will Traynor’s storyline ends there, Louisa Clark have a whole life in front of her </span>
  <span id="freeText6276919956823340697" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Louisa Clark returns!!!</u>
</b><br /><br /><br /><i>This novel is the sequel to “Me Before You”, so you need to read that book first to be able to engage into this one.</i><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>BECAUSE LIFE DOESN’T END LIKE BOOKS</u>
</b><br /><br />I am truly glad that Jojo Moyes, the author, decided to write this sequel, since while <i>Me Before You</i> has a proper closure and you could be totally satisfied there, well, life doesn’t have “endings” like the books, and certainly while Will Traynor’s storyline ends there, Louisa Clark have a whole life in front of her and it was thrilling to know how was it, without having to guess.<br /><br />And also, not only Louisa, but the entire Clark Family, the Traynor Family and even other characters like Patrick and Nathan. All those support characters that you learned to love or hate, all depending of your very personal point of view, all of them, their lives carry on too, and you’ll know what happened with each of them.<br /><br />And you can trust that Louisa Clark’s life is like her clothing…<br /><br />…anything but boring!<br /><br />And since I won't make any spoilers, I only can tell you that you'll have a lot of surprises!<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>PEOPLE GOT OUT, PEOPLE GOT IN</u>
</b><br /><br />Obviously, like in life doesn’t have “endings”, also you never stop to meet new people, and certainly, here, in <i>After You</i>, Louisa Clark will meet several new people, and all of them will make impacts on Louisa’s life, and you have to know that not all impacts are negative, there are positive impacts too.<br /><br />And the best of that?<br /><br />That like in life, you can’t foreseen how each of those new characters will turn in the developing of this sequel, like in life, you just have to be careful, to do your best effort to keep on, but always following your heart and insticts, since at the end of the day…<br /><br />…there is nothing more important than being able to watch yourself in the mirror and being sure that all what you did in the day didn’t cause any hurt to others.<br /><br />Nobody is a saint, but we don’t have to be, only avoiding to provoke suffering without need to any person which doesn’t deserve it.<br /><br />Never is easy, many times the easiest path is too tempting, but only you will know if you’re calling the right decision when stressful situations arise.<br /><br />And nobody has to tell you how to live your own life, since only you would know if you’re truly happy and…<br /><br />…if you’re happy with your decisions and don’t causing sorrow to others…<br /><br />…how much else you really need in your life?<br /><br />When somebody who has been too important in your life, in your heart, is gone, you may think that being happy without that person isn’t respectful for the memory of that person, but that isn’t the case, everybody deserves to be happy and if you keep in your mind and heart the memory of that person, you won’t be “betraying” that person if you find happiness in a new person, even more if you do all what you can (and sometimes even more than that) to protect the legacy of that person which isn’t here anymore.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE PATH TO DO WHAT'S RIGHT</u>
</b><br /><br />The path to do what's right isn't easy, and it's testing, but when you trust that you're doing wha'ts morally right and you can be yourself at ease on the mirror, at the end, it will be worthy.<br /><br />And don’t rush up to judge others, since in most cases, you won’t really know them, what’s in their minds, hearts and souls. Judging is easy. Helping isn’t. <br /><br />If you think that you’re not up to lend a hand, don't do it, don't torture yourself, but then at least don’t judge since that won’t help neither.<br /><br />Nobody expects that you save the world, but as Oskar Schindler found out…<br /><br />…to save a life is to save the world.<br /><br />And not lives needed to save from a physical wound, some lives needed to save from soul wounds and sometimes they are in such dark place that they put themselves beyond of accepting help and they can be testing, but if you think that it's the right thing to do, not matter the outcome, it will be worthy too.<br /><br />Maybe you won’t be in the position to do something as dramatic to save a life, but any positive impact in another’s life…<br /><br />…you’ll never know how much will help others in the future.<br /><br />Nobody will do what you need to do in the world. If you don't do those things, nobody else will do it. You're unique in the world in ways that you wouldn't believe it. For better or worse. It's A Wonderful Life! (and nope, it's not that here you'll have a parallel dimension situation! I just think that the thought that nobody else will do what you must do, it was right to apply here).<br /><br />And again, always think if whatever you do, you’ll be able to watch yourself in the mirror.<br /><br />Since you are the only one able to judge yourself and your own actions.<br /><br />Other people and their actions and repercussions? Only God can judge them.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6276919956823340697" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6262778222825082276">I laughed, I cried, I laughed so hard that I cried, and then I sobbed ridiculously. This book has some of the best examples of female friendship I have ever seen in my life and I absolutely love Lily and Lou's friendship. So beautiful! The only problem I had was that near the end of the book something SUPER DRAMATIC happens that didn't need to happen and I was just like ugggggh.</span>

<div id="review_1719436651" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1719436651" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1719436651?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=non-ya">non-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=nope">nope</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=couldn-t-wait-to-read">couldn-t-wait-to-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1719436651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14106742143950321916">(This review contains spoilers for Me Before You.)<br/>With unexpected sequels like this one, I suppose it comes down to whether the sequel adds anything to the original. And I’m going to say this one doesn’t.<br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2017/03/20/after-you-review/'>https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483808451ra/21651429.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I recognize the temptation to write a follow-up to Me Before You. That one smashed it, a rare combination of being a Goodreads ratings darling and having commercial/bestseller success. It’s an absolute goldmine. Of course you’d want to beat that particular</span>
  <span id="freeText14106742143950321916" style="display:none">(This review contains spoilers for Me Before You.)<br>With unexpected sequels like this one, I suppose it comes down to whether the sequel adds anything to the original. And I’m going to say this one doesn’t.<br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2017/03/20/after-you-review/">https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483808451ra/21651429.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I recognize the temptation to write a follow-up to Me Before You. That one smashed it, a rare combination of being a Goodreads ratings darling and having commercial/bestseller success. It’s an absolute goldmine. Of course you’d want to beat that particular dead horse. But I don’t have to appreciate your treatment of that poor equine corpse. (And compare those GR ratings - a lot of readers don’t like it either.)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483808451ra/21651430.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>”But that’s just a fairy-tale ending, isn’t it? Man dies, everyone learns something, moves on, creates something wonderful out of his death.”</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483808451ra/21651431.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>An interesting sentence, that. Its intention is to explain the “need” for a sequel, when, in actuality, it’s making the reader feel guilty for loving the first book. Or at least liking it enough to appreciate its follow-up. I was already sensitive to criticisms of the first book, because I hate liking things that could be problematic in any way. (I didn’t even like the movie, which drew the most ire, and I <i>still</i> feel guilty!)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483808451ra/21651432.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Let me explain my love for Me Before You so I can carefully outline my qualms against this follow-up. Me Before You is quite the love story - I don’t feel emotions very often, and I <i>definitely</i> felt something while reading that book. It made a claim for the humanity of assisted suicide, which is a cause I believe in. And it had a nice theme - we only have one life and we need to live it.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1406056912ra/10495269.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book was 400 pages of the latter, again. Because apparently, the reader isn’t intelligent enough to infer that Louisa Clark mourned, and then made her way to living her fullest life. No, we had to follow along as she monotonously ambled through it. There was no grand love story. (Though there was a forced and un-interesting one alarmingly close to the first book.) The attempt at social-issue appeal was an alarmingly outdated subplot on a housewife’s introduction to basic feminism that bordered on circus sideshow in sheer goofiness. Also, some heavy-handed looks at, like, violence? Maybe gangs? I think I detected what may have been a soon-removed effort to discuss mental illness.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483808451ra/21651433.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And there’s the kicker - this book should, at its core, discuss grief and mourning. Instead, it inserts truisms. Its “Moving On Support Group” is a joke, cycled through a repetitive storyline in the hopes it’ll make sense when Lou makes progress. (It doesn’t.)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382070783ra/5640971.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This made me realize that I don’t even <i>like</i> Louisa Clark. I liked Will Traynor. Or did I? I liked their romance. Or did I? The worst kind of sequel is one that casts an uncertain light on your feelings for the first book. God, I’m so unhappy right now.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433034738ra/15041554.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I feel bad for my family - in day two (three?) of my post-wisdom tooth surgery recovery, I dragged my swollen face about the house complaining about how I didn’t like this book. My mom, a fellow Moyes appreciator, wisely told me to stop reading it. I can’t, I said, filled with mistaken confidence. The entire appeal of this book is in the promise of character development. HA, HA, HA. GOOD ONE, ME.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483808569ra/21651450.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Lou completes this book worse off than in Me Before You - even in her state of quasi-full recovery, she’s lost her light, her large personality. She’s like an entirely different character. Really, this felt like reading a wholly different world from the first book.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1482548253ra/21526910.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Most of the story is Lou’s <s>obsession with</s> devotion to a sixteen year old <s>miscreant</s> misunderstood lovebug. She hangs on this girl’s every word, smokes weed when she’s asked, forgives a series of misdeeds ranging in severity - all for a girl she doesn’t know. She sums up her thoughts on her participation in the pot-smoking with: “Afterward, I couldn’t believe I had been manipulated by a sixteen-year-old. But Lily was like the cool girl in class, the one you found yourself trying to impress.” From a thirty year old. From a grown ass woman.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483808451ra/21651435.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Looks like I’m not leaving the ruination of some of my favorite books by shitty follow-ups in 2016.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483808451ra/21651436.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Bottom line: If you loved Me Before You like I did, swaddle yourself in that love. Ignore negative reviews, and <b>especially</b> ignore the existence of this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14106742143950321916" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1212729881" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1212729881" />
    <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters"><img alt="Elyse  Walters" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514246949p2/597461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1212729881?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elyse  Walters" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters">Elyse  Walters</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780698411418" href="/book/show/25020381-after-you">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1212729881" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6479437872638418843">At the start of "After You", I told my friend Iris..."well, it's not as bad as I was expecting". I never thought it was a great idea to write a sequel to "Me Before You"...<br/>a 'favorite' book by many people.... drawing conversations about 'the ending' from people all over the globe. For one thing, "Me Before You" was never written 'with' the intention of their being a follow up. "After You", was an "After Thought". <br/>Expecting a complete plane crash...I found myself interested & engaged in the begin</span>
  <span id="freeText6479437872638418843" style="display:none">At the start of "After You", I told my friend Iris..."well, it's not as bad as I was expecting". I never thought it was a great idea to write a sequel to "Me Before You"...<br />a 'favorite' book by many people.... drawing conversations about 'the ending' from people all over the globe. For one thing, "Me Before You" was never written 'with' the intention of their being a follow up. "After You", was an "After Thought". <br />Expecting a complete plane crash...I found myself interested &amp; engaged in the beginning -keeping an opened mind. <br />Louisa has an accident early in this story ...( so I was hooked)... however from the get-go, I kept asking myself though, "why did the author start "After You" 19 months 'after' Will died in "Me Before You"? To the extent Louisa was still grieving, it would have been more realistic if Jojo Moyes began this story about 6 or 7 months after his death. <br />By 19 months ...her whining should have decreased substantially. Besides, Louisa only knew Will for about 6 months in "Me Before You". The real power of "Me Before You", was *Will's* story anyway...so the author was going to need to generate almost a complete new story line for Louisa. <br />I saw potential .....( starting with Louisa's accident), .....not like Will's....but there was substance, in which to move the plot forward. ( in the beginning)...yet the story moved on so fast....( there was never any real agony that we felt for Louisa...she would recover quickly)...<br />Moyes wrote several incomplete plots, with a variety of characters.... with too many storylines. <br /><br />Basically, this novel lacked a powerful focus!!! <br />It lacked powerful - fresh- insights! ( something that made "Me Before You", brilliant). <br />It was like an 'ok' meal. ( filled your belly at the time, but not one that you'll probably think about - one way or another - good or bad - much again).<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6479437872638418843" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1600435781" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1600435781" />
    <a title="Megan Johnson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31853583-megan-johnson"><img alt="Megan Johnson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523045365p2/31853583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1600435781?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan Johnson" href="/user/show/31853583-megan-johnson">Megan Johnson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25041504-after-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31853583-megan-johnson?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1600435781" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6364940432835216339">After reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You__Me_Before_You___1_' title='Me Before You (Me Before You, #1) by Jojo Moyes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Me Before You</a>, I couldn't help but want to keep the story going. Lou was charming and understandably heartbroken, and despite knowing that sequels rarely live up to the original, I decided to give it a go. <br/><br/>After You is so different from Me Before You that it often felt like a standalone more than a sequel...which was both good and bad. It was good in that I didn't feel like I had to spend the length of the read constantly comparing the two in order to determine whether it was a goo</span>
  <span id="freeText6364940432835216339" style="display:none">After reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You__Me_Before_You___1_" title="Me Before You (Me Before You, #1) by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a>, I couldn't help but want to keep the story going. Lou was charming and understandably heartbroken, and despite knowing that sequels rarely live up to the original, I decided to give it a go. <br /><br />After You is so different from Me Before You that it often felt like a standalone more than a sequel...which was both good and bad. It was good in that I didn't feel like I had to spend the length of the read constantly comparing the two in order to determine whether it was a good follow up. But I also felt a bit let down. I had become so attached to those original characters that to be thrown in with a seemingly new group was maybe a bit weird. <br /><br />That being said, I found this book to be thoroughly enjoyable. I wouldn't, though, put it in the same class as it's predecessor. It's different, it's a fabulous story, but I didn't feel the emotional pull or the need to devour it that I had before. <br /><br />Quite honestly, I think I give this one a hard time because my expectations were so high. <br /><br /><b>What did I think?:</b> This book is far from a disappointment. It's a fun, easy read and if you loved Me Before You, you'll likely enjoy this one too. It wasn't at all what I expected, but that didn't take away from the enjoyment of it. It did feel a bit rushed to fit in a second storyline almost, but since I enjoyed this story as well, I really didn't mind too much. <br /><br /><b>Who should read it?:</b> If you've read Me Before You, I definitely think you should give this one a read. It's a fun story that will have those that loved it's previous book will love knowing what happens afterward. <br /><br /><br /><br /><a href="http://www.tipsywriter.com" rel="nofollow noopener">WEBSITE</a> | <a href="http://www.twitter.com/tipsy_writer" rel="nofollow noopener">TWITTER</a> | <a href="http://www.facebook.com/tipsywriter" rel="nofollow noopener">FACEBOOK</a> | <a href="http://www.instagram.com/tipsywriter" rel="nofollow noopener">INSTAGRAM</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6364940432835216339" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
