<div id="review_1212787878" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1212787878" />
    <a title="Arlene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene"><img alt="Arlene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347048609p2/1746727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1212787878?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arlene" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene">Arlene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525426592" href="/book/show/24941288-after-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1212787878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12440495059482990223"><i>You are going to feel uncomfortable in your new world for a bit. It always does feel strange to be knocked out of your comfort zone… There is hunger in you, Clark. You just buried it, like most people do. ~Will...</i><br/><br/>Nothing short of beautiful! An emotionally charged story about healing and learning to believe in yourself after a painful loss. I am in love with this story!<br/><br/><b>After You</b> was definitely my most anticipated releases for 2015, and it absolutely didn’t disappoint one bit! I fell in love with </span>
  <span id="freeText12440495059482990223" style="display:none"><i>You are going to feel uncomfortable in your new world for a bit. It always does feel strange to be knocked out of your comfort zone… There is hunger in you, Clark. You just buried it, like most people do. ~Will...</i><br /><br />Nothing short of beautiful! An emotionally charged story about healing and learning to believe in yourself after a painful loss. I am in love with this story!<br /><br /><b>After You</b> was definitely my most anticipated releases for 2015, and it absolutely didn’t disappoint one bit! I fell in love with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You" title="Me Before You by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a> and remember wanting just a few more chapters of Louisa’s life after that climactic ending. Well, the sequel <b>After You</b> feels like the epilogue I desperately needed!<br /><br />This story picks up about eighteen months after the ending of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You" title="Me Before You by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a>. I’ll try to keep this as spoiler-free as possible, but to get straight to the point, Louisa is truly struggling with moving on from the events that unfolded with Will Traynor. She’s working at a job she has no interest in and is floundering from day to day just trying to keep herself from an impending downward spiral.<br /><br />After a fateful night where she suffers from a horrible accident, she returns to her hometown to recover and there begins her attempt to heal from her wounds both physical and emotional. Through her recovery, she meets a cast of wonderful characters that slowly become the foundation for her new life.<br /><br />There were so many layers to this novel that only created a feeling of being fully invested in Louisa Clark’s life. After Will Traynor’s fateful decision in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You" title="Me Before You by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a>, we get to journey with Louisa during her road to recovery. She meets Lily Houghton-Miller and Sam Fielding, who I absolutely adored because in their own ways, they brought back the Lou I knew from the first book. I appreciated how Lily challenged Lou to try and move on without a feeling of guilt clouding her every move. I also enjoyed seeing Sam break down Lou’s walls and teach her to love again. Beautiful set of characters that were a perfect addition to this story!<br /><br />There was also another set of secondary characters that added a whole new flavor to this novel. <i>The Moving On Circle</i> was a breath of fresh air! Daphne, William, Natasha, Fred, Marc and Jake each complemented the story with their own journey toward recovery. I enjoyed their therapy sessions that revealed their insecurities, fears and hopes. It was all so serious, yet shared with a level of brevity that kept the story flowing with ease.<br /><br />Louisa’s journey wouldn’t be complete without a few scenes with her quirky but loveable family! Adored them! This family was absolutely flawed to perfection! It was quite clear they cared about Louisa and her struggles. It’s nice to experience a story where family is still one of the most important things in life. <br /><br />Finally, the spotlight deservedly belongs to Louisa Clark. Throughout this entire journey, she showed compassion, bravery, determination and heart. There wasn’t one moment where I faltered in my allegiance to her plight. I wanted her to become not only the Louisa we knew and loved in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You" title="Me Before You by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a>, but an even better version of that character as she worked hard to recover from a painful experience. Lou has become my favorite female character of 2015! Loved her!!<br /><br />There were moments and passages in this story that truly hit me hard. JoJo Moyes clearly has a skillful way of cutting to the core of her readers’ emotional pockets with quick punches that leave you breathless for air. <b>After You</b> had many of those moments of brilliance. Overall, I believe fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You" title="Me Before You by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a> will enjoy journeying with Louisa Clark as she learns to fall in love and believe in herself again. Beautiful… absolutely beautiful!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12440495059482990223" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I'll try to forget. For me Lou & Will's story ended with the last page of <b>Me before you</b>. I don't think we needed a new story.<br/><br/>I'm not saying this is bad, it's Jojo - it can't, but it just kind of ruined part of what I imagined for Lou after the end of the first book.   <span id="freeText13199859923814882245" style="display:none"><b>Review after the read</b><br><br>3 - Because I love Jojo Moyes - Stars<br><br><br>I'm sorry, I'm very sorry to say that I would've preferred that this book was never born. I'll try to forget. For me Lou &amp; Will's story ended with the last page of <b>Me before you</b>. I don't think we needed a new story.<br><br>I'm not saying this is bad, it's Jojo - it can't, but it just kind of ruined part of what I imagined for Lou after the end of the first book. And every single time I read Will's name in this my heart skipped a beat, and I confessed I was a little bit annoyed with all those characters, it was like if they were "intruding" our story. And I'm sorry to say that the most annoying and boring part was Lily. I couldn't care less about her. And surprisingly my favorite part/character was Sam, the one that I should've hate but instead I adored.<br><br>I really don't know what to say about this book, probably I shouldn't have read it, but I couldn't resist. So, if you loved the first book and you're not sure about this, I'd say that you can easily skip this one and continue to imagine what you want about their lives... because it's probably better of what really happened. But if you really want to read it, then read it like if this is a new story and you don't know who Will was, even if it's impossible, you have to forget everything you knew about them.<br><br>Anyway, if you read it prepare your tissues, it's always Jojo Moyes ;)<br><br><br><br>------------------------<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424989770ra/13827994.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm gonna die.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424989770i/13827995.png" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm happy<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424989770ra/13827996.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>and scared<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424989973ra/13828033.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>because I can already imagine what's going to happen... to me.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424989973ra/13828034.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424990098ra/13828095.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424990098ra/13828096.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm not ready for this.<br><br></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1768296214" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1768296214" />
    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7365405-james"><img alt="James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522094190p2/7365405.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1768296214?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/7365405-james">James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25041504-after-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=1-fiction">1-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=3-multi-book-series">3-multi-book-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1768296214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2420924929917877980">3 stars to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/281810.Jojo_Moyes' title='Jojo Moyes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jojo Moyes</a>'s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25041504.After_You__Me_Before_You___2_' title='After You (Me Before You, #2) by Jojo Moyes' rel='nofollow noopener'>After You</a>, the follow-up to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15340802.Me_Before_You' title='Me Before You' rel='nofollow noopener'>Me Before You</a>, which was a very popular book made into a movie earlier this year. The "After You" sequel is good (not as good), but for a different reason. Many folks complained about the need for this second book, and with the first one being made into a movie, it may have been a required follow-up as opposed to a story that yearned to be told... either case, I did enjoy it. Let's dive in...<br/> <br/><b>
  <u>Story</u>
</b><br/>The book opens about 18 months after the fi</span>
  <span id="freeText2420924929917877980" style="display:none">3 stars to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/281810.Jojo_Moyes" title="Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Jojo Moyes</a>'s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25041504.After_You__Me_Before_You___2_" title="After You (Me Before You, #2) by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">After You</a>, the follow-up to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15340802.Me_Before_You" title="Me Before You" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a>, which was a very popular book made into a movie earlier this year. The "After You" sequel is good (not as good), but for a different reason. Many folks complained about the need for this second book, and with the first one being made into a movie, it may have been a required follow-up as opposed to a story that yearned to be told... either case, I did enjoy it. Let's dive in...<br> <br><b>
  <u>Story</u>
</b><br>The book opens about 18 months after the first one ends, which was when her patient and soul-mate, Will Traynor, committed suicide. (If you are reading this review, it's not really a spoiler as that's the whole point of Me Before You -- how will she handle the tragedy of being with him... and if you haven't read Book 1, stop now and go back and read it even before this review of Book 2. You can also check out my Book 1 review in the link below).<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479503178ra/21199595.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> Are you listening? :P<br><br>Louisa (the girl who fell for Will) has been on the outs with her family due to her role in Wil's suicide, and she took a year off to travel and try to move forward. Of course, it never happens, and she goes back to the quiet and sheltered life she had before she met him. When she accidentally falls off her roof, it sets into motion several challenges for her to face. Some think she tried to kill herself. Some think she is rotting away her life. She goes back to a very sad job where she's yelled at by a nasty boss all the time. She tries to get better by going to a self-help group for people affected by a loved one who died. She meets the ambulance medic who saved her after the fall. She gets a job offer to go to NYC. And she meets Lily, the secret daughter Will had that no one ever knew about. While Louisa tries to figure out her life, she learns all the lessons she needs to be able to move on... but when it all comes together in the end, and she has to make a choice on her own future, will she be able to? (And that's for you to find out when you read the book... I can't give a spoiler away, right?)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491602086ra/22427879.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>Strengths</u>
</b><br>1. Lou is a fantastic character. She's flawed which makes her real. She's whiny yet she stands up for herself. She's smart and she makes dumb decisions. She's got potential but she lets it waste. We can all find a piece of Lou's personality in our own, which makes reading about her and understanding her actions all the more interesting... because you can question whether you would have done the same thing or made a different decision. She's quite relate-able... on may levels.<br><br>2. The plot is great, especially as a follow-up to Me Before You. It could have gone in many directions, e.g. a trial/lawsuit from the family or the government for her role in his death, a barrage of press harassment, the anger of her family, etc. Instead, the book gives us an 18 month break from the last one, and its inherent immediate reactions to the death, which also allows the reader time to grieve and want to see Lou move on. So... the plot had room to be widely open, but needed to be connected to the first one -- a mysterious unknown daughter -- while over-played in movies -- isn't so common in books... and I enjoyed watching it unfold. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491602086ra/22427880.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>3. It's witty. Dialogue is on-target. Characters are bold but also complex. The story is consistent. It holds interest. It retains some of the sadness of the first book but brings you to a middle / average level of how you feel about the pain... and leaves you thinking "these people are real." And that's what I enjoy in a book. I don't want to feel harsh and judgmental of character actions, or find myself in love with something perfect that doesn't really exist... yes, literature is often supposed to take you out of reality and into something fantastical where you feel magical... but for me, the very nature of fiction does that -- I enjoy the great sweeping arcs of magic, but when the story is simple and beautiful, it's even better.<br><br><b>
  <u>Suggestions</u>
</b><br>I don't believe there should have been a follow-up to Me Before You, and I'm a serial-fictionist... as well as a lexiconnoisseur neologist (apparently, I make up words like serial-fictionist). The first one was so good as a stand-alone, I don't want to compare anything to it with the same story and author being involved. Perhaps if I just picked up After You, I wouldn't have enjoyed it as much without knowing what happened to Lou in Book 1. Book 2 (After You) is a good story with good writing, but there wasn't anything special about it, hence why I have it a 3. If I hadn't witnessed her struggle in the previous book, it wouldn't have been as powerful in this book to watch her recovery.<br><br><b>
  <u>Final Thoughts</u>
</b><br>So... with it getting a 3, and with me not having anything truly remarkable to say about it, I'd recommend it to folks under certain conditions:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491602086ra/22427881.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>1. If you read Me Before You, you should read After You. If you love Louisa and her family, then why wouldn't you want to read another 350 pages about their life... it's like having a friend who lives far away and just happens to be in your town and may never be again for years. It's there... It's a day's read. It's enjoyable. It just isn't the same as it was the first go around. But you still want to know "how is that friend of mine different these days..." - so go see that friend.<br><br>2. If you love the author's style, read After You. It's a well-written book and has a few good characters you will root for. <br><br>3. If you can accept the original is the best, and know that you won't always get the same vibe and attraction to its successors, then you probably have an open enough mind to check out what happened in her later years.<br><br>But if you are looking for an amazing follow-up with an absolute blockbuster of a story and ending to Lou's life... you will be somewhat disappointed. After You is a slice of what happens to her in a 3 month period set nearly 2 years after the first one ends. It's nice. It's a good read. But you won't walk away with the same level of emotions as you did with Me Before You.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>About Me</u>
  </i>
</b><br>For those new to me or my reviews... here's the scoop: I read A LOT. I write A LOT. And now I blog A LOT. First the book review goes on Goodreads, and then I send it on over to my WordPress blog at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://thisismytruthnow.com">https://thisismytruthnow.com</a>, where you'll also find TV &amp; Film reviews, the revealing and introspective 365 Daily Challenge and lots of blogging about places I've visited all over the world. And you can find all my social media profiles to get the details on the who/what/when/where and my pictures. <br><br>Leave a comment and let me know what you think. Vote in the poll and ratings. Thanks for stopping by.</span>

Only cause it can't live up to book number one, nor should it have to. <br /><br />I was absolutely impressed and delighted with this sequel. As we all know, this was one hard act to follow. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/281810.Jojo_Moyes" title="Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Jojo Moyes</a> had not planned to offer a follow up to the perfect <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You__Me_Before_You___1_" title="Me Before You (Me Before You, #1) by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a>, but as Lou and Will were so wonderful to read about, we were lucky that she decided to write again for us.<br /><br />My thoughts are that this does not have to live up to its predecessor, it’s its own story, and I loved it. Things did fall neatly into place at times throughout, but I was happy this was the case. It was sweet, nice and all things good. <br /><br />I recommend this continuing tale, it's a lovely story written very well, and I was hooked from start to finish. This lady is a talented author and I’m glad I’ve read a lot of her work - even better that I have lots more waiting for me!<br /><br />Those who've not read this author should jump on the band wagon quick smart.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17383640413561879433"><br/>So disappointing....<br/><br/><br/>Jojo Moyes is one of my top favorite authors, I have loved every book I have read of hers up until this one. Me Before You is in my top five favorite books of all time, I still get emotional just thinking about that story. I wish so much that I could say this novel was a worthy sequel, but to me it just wasn't, not even close. This sequel in my opinion, is the exact reason <b> that kind of perfection just shouldn't be messed with.</b> Me Before You was written as a stand alone, and </span>
  <span id="freeText17383640413561879433" style="display:none"><br>So disappointing....<br><br><br>Jojo Moyes is one of my top favorite authors, I have loved every book I have read of hers up until this one. Me Before You is in my top five favorite books of all time, I still get emotional just thinking about that story. I wish so much that I could say this novel was a worthy sequel, but to me it just wasn't, not even close. This sequel in my opinion, is the exact reason <b> that kind of perfection just shouldn't be messed with.</b> Me Before You was written as a stand alone, and after reading this one, I honestly feel it should have been left that way. I know that Moyes wrote this story in response to her fans who wanted more of this story that they loved, but that doesn't mean it was a good idea to go there. Me Before You had my all time favorite epilogue, and I can say that re-reading that evoked more emotion from me than this entire sequel did. After You was not only unnecessary, but it felt contrived, and to be honest, I'm sorry that I read it.<br><br>On a positive note I am looking forward to the film. I plan to watch it in my own house on dvd after everyone else is in bed, with a box of tissues, a gallon of chocolate ice cream, and maybe some wine.<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/XHAH4ED" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443628253i/16387252.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>*sniff* that was my favorite scene from the first book.<br><br>Please don't open this unless you want spoilers. Here's my spoilerish emotional outburst, or the rest of my review.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><br>My main issue with the book was that I couldn't stand the Lily story line. Nothing about that felt authentic to me. I felt like it was just a cheesy way to try to keep Will and his family in the story. If you hate that part of the story, it's really hard to like the book because it really takes over. And the fact that it was Lily who was there when she fell? Oh, brother. And holy hell, how many different characters did she need to bring into this? I don't care about Will's father either.<br><br>Also, I think I just missed Will. I liked Sam, but I just really didn't feel their connection. This was supposed to be about Louisa's journey after Will, and she wasn't even the focus of the book.<br><br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Thanks to the girls from the br, I hope you will like it better than I did! :)<br><br>*edit 10/1/15 this is a review written by my friend Maida who so perfectly summed this up.<br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1213488967?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525426592" href="/book/show/24941288-after-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=arc-electronic">arc-electronic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=from-netgalley">from-netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=2015">2015</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=genre-contemporary">genre-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=age-adult">age-adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1348241329" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11447442206161410907">An Electronic Advance Reader Copy was provided by the publisher via NetGalley for review.<br/><br/>There's this version in my head where the actions from the previous book Me Before You is irrelevant. Readers who have read the book know exactly what I'm talking about, that moment in the end where things could have ended differently. Way differently. And then I realized there was going to be a sequel. How would life go on after everything that happened? How would each and every one of the characters move o</span>
  <span id="freeText11447442206161410907" style="display:none">An Electronic Advance Reader Copy was provided by the publisher via NetGalley for review.<br /><br />There's this version in my head where the actions from the previous book Me Before You is irrelevant. Readers who have read the book know exactly what I'm talking about, that moment in the end where things could have ended differently. Way differently. And then I realized there was going to be a sequel. How would life go on after everything that happened? How would each and every one of the characters move on? I couldn't fully comprehend the need for a sequel, but my friend pushed me to read it, so I ended up requesting it on NetGalley. <br /><br />I knew from the moment I read the first paragraph I wouldn't stick to reading it for too long. This one would be read quickly and devoured. Hoping that I would be released from the clutches of emotional turmoil Me Before You entailed. I was wrong of course. Jojo just knows how to stick her hands into your heart and wrench it. There's one part where I couldn't bare to read that I literally left my iPad on the table for twenty-four hours because I had to come to grips with what just happened or what was said. It brought up all the emotions that I felt for the characters and I couldn't help but cry. Yep, I knew I wouldn't last long. Moyes delivers a story that will have you nodding your head along and making sure you'll be the cheerleader the characters need. I love her writing. I will forever cherish this book only because I remember feeling all the feels for one particular character. I have to remind myself that Will isn't real, but the thing is, this person could be anyone in my life, and in a little way it could even be me.<br /><br />Get ready to be brought into a new whirlwind romance, but that doesn't stop there either. There's more family, friendship and obviously a lot of healing needed to be done. This is the story of what happens after someone you love has passed away. Don't say I didn't warn you that it has its twists and turns.</span>

    <a title="Christina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14066678-christina"><img alt="Christina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481826762p2/14066678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1523808458?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina" href="/user/show/14066678-christina">Christina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25041504-after-you">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1523808458" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17549017242833622080">4 stars!<br/><br/><b>***This will contain spoilers for Me Before You, for those who haven't read it yet***</b><br/><br/><b>"Sometimes I look at the lives of the people around me and I wonder if we aren't all destined to leave a trail of damage. It's not just your mum and dad who fuck you up. I gazed around me, like someone suddenly handed clear glasses, and I saw that pretty much everyone bore the brutal imprint of love, whether it was lost, whipped away from them, or simply vanished into a grave. Will had done it to all of </b></span>
  <span id="freeText17549017242833622080" style="display:none">4 stars!<br /><br /><b>***This will contain spoilers for Me Before You, for those who haven't read it yet***</b><br /><br /><b>"Sometimes I look at the lives of the people around me and I wonder if we aren't all destined to leave a trail of damage. It's not just your mum and dad who fuck you up. I gazed around me, like someone suddenly handed clear glasses, and I saw that pretty much everyone bore the brutal imprint of love, whether it was lost, whipped away from them, or simply vanished into a grave. Will had done it to all of us, I saw now. He hadn't meant to, but even in simply refusing to live, he had."</b><br /><br />This is the sequel to Me Before You. I was pretty nervous going into this. MBY didn't have the cliche happily ever after ending, but after my re-read of it, I ended up liking the way things turned out. I felt good about Lou's future prospects. Enter in this sequel...<br /><br />It's been 18 months since Louisa lost Will. She spent the first little bit of time traveling around Europe before using her money from Will to buy a flat in London. She is bartending in an airport bar and just basically going through life day by day. She's stopped dressing like her old self and doesn't have much contact with her family. A drunken accident forces Lou to return home to her parents house. She feels like she's right back at square one and some members of the local community won't let her forget the past...to them, she is still that girl who stood aside and did nothing as another willfully ended his life. She is basically in a dark place, internally.<br /><br /><b>"Now, when I read newspaper stories about the bank teller who had stolen a fortune, the woman who had killed her child, the sibling who had disappeared, I found myself not shuddering in horror, as I might once have, but wondering instead at the part of the story that hadn't made it into print. What i felt with them was a weird kinship. I was tainted. The world around me knew it. Worse, I had started to know it too."</b><br /><br />Once she is healed enough to return to London, she goes under the condition that she will attend meetings with the Moving On Support Group ( through which she meets Sam, the paramedic that had a hand in saving her ).Then a very unexpected figure from Will's past, a girl named Lily, comes barging into her life, disrupting her plans and propelling her in a new direction, giving her a new purpose. Lou will learn to deal with a bratty teenager and possibly even learn to open up her heart to love again.<br /><br />I'll admit, this went in a very different direction than I was expecting. I know firsthand that people deal with grief in many different ways and for varying lengths of time, but I really was very frustrated by Lou for a lot of this book. And Lily...I wanted to just smack her ( though not as much as I wanted to strangle Lily's mom )! Even when the reasons behind her brattiness and behavior were explained, I still wanted to tell her how stupid she had been. I didnt really start to warm up to her character until the last few chapters. So I'm torn...I would've been happy with just Me Before You's ending, assuming that Lou led a big life with a lot of adventures after having her outlook on life changed by her time spent with Will. But I'm happy I read the sequel, which painted a more realistic picture of Lou's life after, how Will's death affected her and the rest of his family as well. I do feel like the ending of After You opened up more questions rather than closure for me, mainly concerning Lou and Sam and their budding relationship...It makes me almost curious if there might even be another book about Louisa Clark in the future. I didn't quite like this as much as MBY, but it was good, had some humorous moments, and had some tender moments too. Would recommend to fans of Me Before You.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17549017242833622080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1385205941" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1385205941" />
    <a title="Jasmine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine"><img alt="Jasmine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582366251p2/21803154.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1385205941?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine">Jasmine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525426592" href="/book/show/24941288-after-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=movie-based">movie-based</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=will-reread">will-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=just-fine">just-fine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=light-read">light-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=practical-methods">practical-methods</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=skimming-through">skimming-through</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=happy-ending">happy-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=positive-ideas">positive-ideas</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1385205941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15010272558556724531"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>You never know what will happen, when you fall from a great height.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>
  <u>***Actual rating: 3.5/5 relieving stars.***</u>
</b><br/><br/>I didn't plan on reading this today, or any time soon, but when I suddenly had an entire afternoon in a bookstore, AND this beautiful book happened to be there in front of me...<i>how could I resist?</i> So I quickly skimmed through the entire book and gladly, many parts of the story caught my undivided attention.<br/><br/>Apparently, we followed Louisa Clark's life <i>without</i> Will's company</span>
  <span id="freeText15010272558556724531" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>You never know what will happen, when you fall from a great height.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>
  <u>***Actual rating: 3.5/5 relieving stars.***</u>
</b><br /><br />I didn't plan on reading this today, or any time soon, but when I suddenly had an entire afternoon in a bookstore, AND this beautiful book happened to be there in front of me...<i>how could I resist?</i> So I quickly skimmed through the entire book and gladly, many parts of the story caught my undivided attention.<br /><br />Apparently, we followed Louisa Clark's life <i>without</i> Will's company and even after 18 months, she found herself unable to truly live her life to the fullest. For me, a majority of the plot was too dramatic and full of so-so events among the new characters(like Lily and Sam); however, <b>another small part of it reminded me of our beloved Will Traynor and immediately brought back bittersweet, heartfelt emotions to me.</b> That's why I liked this book. Besides, <b>I loved how much stronger, tougher, braver Lou had become and how she eventually learned to let bygone be bygone.</b> <br /><br />As for the romance, I personally think it was a little bit abrupt. That is, Lou seemed to just trying to distract herself from facing the music so she was simply playing <i>his</i> heart and didn't really mean to take it seriously. Thankfully, both of them plucked up the courage to spill out secrets and deepest thoughts to each other; as a result, a firm relationship was established. By the way, how their love turned from utter excuses to something real moved me a lot because only the kind of love enduring all the hardship and trials would last longer.<br /><br />All in all, this isn't as disappointing for me as for others, though I do prefer the first book more. Enough said, it's still a highly-recommended series for all of you!<br />Here's my most favorite, most satisfying part of the book:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Lily was the first to step forward, holding her white helium balloon. She lifted her arm, then as an afterthought, stooped and picked a tiny blue cornflower from one of her pots and tied it carefully to the string. Then she straightened, raised her hand, and, after the smallest hesitation, released the balloon.</i>
</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <i>I watched as Steven Traynor followed, saw Della's gentle squeeze of his arm as he did so. Camilla released hers, then Fred, Sunil, Georgina, her arm linked with her mother's. My mother, Treena, Dad, blowing his nose noisily into his handkerchief, and Sam. We stood in silence on the roof and watched the balloons sail upward, one by one into the clear blue sky, growing smaller and smaller until they were somewhere infinite, unseen.</i>
</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I let mine go.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><u>Anecdote</u><br />When I found this on the bookshelf, I was too excited to bother seeking a comfy seat in the reading area, so I simply stood in the corner and buried my nose in the book. After what felt like an hour, a pretty foreign girl walked toward me, pointing to the book in my hands and asked me where I found it. Then I took her to the shelf and she was, obviously, more excited than I was when seeing the exact book she was looking for. And guess what? It was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You__Me_Before_You___1_" title="Me Before You (Me Before You, #1) by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a>!!! So I kept telling her how great it was and blah, blah, and she bought it without hesitation. Anyway, I felt extremely good after discussing books with someone in real life and I think we indeed all need some bookish friends anywhere and everywhere. :D</span>
  <a data-text-id="15010272558556724531" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1212106022" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" href="/user/show/1379514-magdalena-aka-a-bookaholic-swede">Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25041504-after-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1379514-magdalena-aka-a-bookaholic-swede?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1212106022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17469015007773764453"><strong>Jojo Moyes</strong> has written at the beginning of this book that she doesn't want anyone writing a review to spoil what happens in<strong> Me Before you</strong>, the first book in the series. And, I fully understand that. So that left me with a choice to either write a review that more or less didn't bring up anything that happens in this book that could spoil the first book or spoiler tag the whole review. I have chosen to write a review that doesn't spoil the book.<br/><br/>First of all, do I want to say that you need to read</span>
  <span id="freeText17469015007773764453" style="display:none"><strong>Jojo Moyes</strong> has written at the beginning of this book that she doesn't want anyone writing a review to spoil what happens in<strong> Me Before you</strong>, the first book in the series. And, I fully understand that. So that left me with a choice to either write a review that more or less didn't bring up anything that happens in this book that could spoil the first book or spoiler tag the whole review. I have chosen to write a review that doesn't spoil the book.<br><br>First of all, do I want to say that you need to read the first book; do not attempt to read this book without having read the first book. Some books are standalone, some aren't.   This one should without a doubt be read after <strong>Me Before you</strong>.<br><br>The book is wonderful. I had no idea about the story before I read the book. No clues about what would happen and that was a real treat not knowing how or if <strong>Moyes</strong> would be able to write a book as gripping as <strong>Me Before You</strong>. She has! I had to fight back tears several times when I read this book, and I pride myself on not being a crier. Lou Clark is such a wonderful character and I loved getting to read about her and her family and friends in another book.<br><br>I loved this book. It was such a treat to get a sequel to <strong>Me Before You</strong>. And, I hope for a third book!<br><br><em>I received this copy from the publisher through NetGalley in return for an honest review! Thank you</em><br><br>************************************<br><br><b>Update 3/9 2015:</b> Approved! I'm amazed, not only that I got the book from NetGalley, but also that it only took a day or two to get approved...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441305587ra/16090997.gif" alt="" width="400" height="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>--------------------------------------------<br><br>Jojo Moyes <a href="https://s2.netgalley.com/catalog/book/69698" rel="nofollow noopener">After You</a> is now on NetGalley<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431118573ra/14793953.gif" alt="" width="400" height="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But you can't request the title yet...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431347211ra/14827401.gif" alt="" width="400" height="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So now I have to wait for it to be available to request...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437680946ra/15614052.gif" alt="" width="400" height="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1212616560" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10651691683167741076"><b>After You</b> is the highly anticipated sequel to <b>Me Before You</b> <i>(do read first)</i> and I so wish I could say that it blew me away. The story is all about <i>letting him go</i> and <i>moving on,</i> a tough topic for sure, but just does not compare to the tremendous impact I experienced after reading <b>Me Before You.</b><p>Without giving away any spoilers, I'll just say the beginning is excellent with the introduction of ambulance Sam, and the unexpected appearance of Lily <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[<i>(Will's troubled daughter)</i> <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoil</a></span></p></span>
  <span id="freeText10651691683167741076" style="display:none"><b>After You</b> is the highly anticipated sequel to <b>Me Before You</b> <i>(do read first)</i> and I so wish I could say that it blew me away. The story is all about <i>letting him go</i> and <i>moving on,</i> a tough topic for sure, but just does not compare to the tremendous impact I experienced after reading <b>Me Before You.</b><p>Without giving away any spoilers, I'll just say the beginning is excellent with the introduction of ambulance Sam, and the unexpected appearance of Lily <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<i>(Will's troubled daughter)</i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> was a surprise for sure, albeit a bit drawn out, but OMGOSH Louisa's family members and their overly inane antics just did not fare well with me.</p><p>Overall, an ok read, but missing the emotional feeling and character connection brought about in <b>Me Before You.</b></p><p>Look forward to more from Jojo Moyes as well as the movie version of <b>MBY.</b></p></span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1212616560">

<div id="review_2503147408" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2503147408" />
    <a title="Rebecca Carter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32917354-rebecca-carter"><img alt="Rebecca Carter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416028750p2/32917354.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2503147408?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca Carter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca Carter" href="/user/show/32917354-rebecca-carter">Rebecca Carter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25235195-after-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32917354-rebecca-carter?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32917354-rebecca-carter?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32917354-rebecca-carter?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32917354-rebecca-carter?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32917354-rebecca-carter?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32917354-rebecca-carter?shelf=humour">humour</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2503147408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18038494160081473406">Incase you somehow missed the fantastic first book - "Me Before You" - "After You" is the follow up. Just as tear jerking and funny as the first, "After You" catches up with Louisa after the events of the first book. We discover how she's coping without Will to care for, and whether she's doing as he instructed her to do - to just live. It's great to catch up and revisit the Traynors and Lou's mad but loving family, and see how they are all coping in the aftermath of Will's decision, as well as </span>
  <span id="freeText18038494160081473406" style="display:none">Incase you somehow missed the fantastic first book - "Me Before You" - "After You" is the follow up. Just as tear jerking and funny as the first, "After You" catches up with Louisa after the events of the first book. We discover how she's coping without Will to care for, and whether she's doing as he instructed her to do - to just live. It's great to catch up and revisit the Traynors and Lou's mad but loving family, and see how they are all coping in the aftermath of Will's decision, as well as meeting some new characters such as the Moving On Circle. <br /><br />Jojo Moyes is one of those authors with a special touch, she can make you tear up on one page and have you giggling on the next. I find her similar in style to Marian Keyes, Moyes is just as capable of tackling meaty serious subjects, yet can also look at the little nuances of life and have you laughing out loud. Or if reading in a public place, attempting to cover up your laughs so as not to look like the loon in the room/on the plane/train/coffee shop...<br /><br />Initially I have to admit i was a little skeptical when I heard there was going to be a follow up to the powerful "Me Before You". I worried any sequel wouldn't live up to the engrossing and moving first book, and was in two minds about bothering to even read it. Sure, there are some "as if" moments where you think that's totally implausible, and it's not quite as hard hitting or emotional as the first book, which was so unique and raw it stayed with me for a while after finishing it. Yet this is still a thoroughly enjoyable read and it works because you want to know how all the characters you got to know in the first book are doing. <br />All in all a great follow up to the first story and I'm looking forward to the third book "Still Me".</span>
  <a data-text-id="18038494160081473406" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780698411418" href="/book/show/25020381-after-you">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2175947847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3617562404932239318">So let’s talk a second about my newfound dabbling in the world of audiobooks. I have long-since learned the words to every single song in the history of the world and wanted something different for my morning commute instead of this . . . . <br/><br/><a href='https://lunapic.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1510155262ra/24392761.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><i>(That is 100% the look my husband gives me when I insist on singing too!)</i><br/><br/>Anywho, please note said commute is still not very long so, at best, I get through one “part” of an audiobook each weekday. Despite having both an e-version as well as a paper versio</span>
  <span id="freeText3617562404932239318" style="display:none">So let’s talk a second about my newfound dabbling in the world of audiobooks. I have long-since learned the words to every single song in the history of the world and wanted something different for my morning commute instead of this . . . . <br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1510155262ra/24392761.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>(That is 100% the look my husband gives me when I insist on singing too!)</i><br><br>Anywho, please note said commute is still not very long so, at best, I get through one “part” of an audiobook each weekday. Despite having both an e-version as well as a paper version of an advanced reader copy of <i>After You</i> for over two years (Dear Publishers, never give me anything because I truly am the worst), I couldn't bring myself to read it. I knew I had to be far enough removed from Will's death in order to give this a chance. When a combination of me finding out a third book in this series was soon to be released as well as the audio popping up as both available and recommended to me on the library website I figured what the hell - it was probably time to bite the bullet.<br><br>I had every intention of giving <i>After You</i> 2 Stars because Jo Jo Moyes obviously has a ginormo set of cajones to even <i>attempt</i> to follow up the perfection of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/599784911?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a>. But then <b>ELEVEN FARKING DAYS</b> of listening went by (I know my reading log doesn’t reflect that, but it’s because I’m stupid and forgot to add it) and everything that was magic about the first book was tainted and cheapened and Louisa wasn’t adorable and quirky, but instead insufferable and pretty much a failure at being a grown-up and then Lily (FUCKING LILY!) showed up and I have never wanted to smack the crap out of a child as much as I did her little entitled ass and all of the men were vile and WTF happened Jo Jo – your husband cheat on you or something?!?!?!?! Not all men are awful FFS! Anyway, this was just gross. I am crossing my fingers that this was the “filler” book (although 100,000,000% unnecessary) in Lou’s story so she can get here happily ever after in #3. This one, though???? <br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1510155262ra/24392762.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>On a positive note, the narrator (Anna Acton) had the most pleasant voice and I would love to listen to her read again. Just not a big stinking pile of turd like this one.</i> <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3617562404932239318" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52207144"><img alt="♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568965358p2/52207144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1544730087?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ" href="/user/show/52207144">♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780698411418" href="/book/show/25020381-after-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=2018-reading-challenge">2018-reading-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1544730087" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9019432324017319775"><u>3 Moving on ★'s</u> <br/><br/><i>“You’re going to feel uncomfortable in your new world for a bit. It always does feel strange to be knocked out of your comfort zone . . . There is a hunger in you, Clark. A fearlessness. You just buried it, like most people do. Just live well. Just live.”</i><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524792214ra/25440067.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1524792214i/25440068._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Sadly "After You" was just well... It was an okay read! I was initially very excited about reading this because I completely adored <i>Me Before You.</i> But it was severely lacking :( It was really quite boring, with a few funny bits t</span>
  <span id="freeText9019432324017319775" style="display:none"><u>3 Moving on ★'s</u> <br><br><i>“You’re going to feel uncomfortable in your new world for a bit. It always does feel strange to be knocked out of your comfort zone . . . There is a hunger in you, Clark. A fearlessness. You just buried it, like most people do. Just live well. Just live.”</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524792214ra/25440067.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1524792214i/25440068._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sadly "After You" was just well... It was an okay read! I was initially very excited about reading this because I completely adored <i>Me Before You.</i> But it was severely lacking :( It was really quite boring, with a few funny bits tossed in. Or maybe, it's because I loved Will Traynor from the first book so much and it just wasn't the same without his charisma. It was all pretty predictable and the romance felt kinda stiff up against <i>Me Before You</i>. But I guess that'd be pretty hard to top. <i>Me Before You</i> was such a heart-wrenching, cry your eyes out for a straight week kinda book. It had left me devastatingly broken and has stuck with me all this time! Over all i'm left feeling pretty disappointed! I know fans were dying to know, Whats next for Lou Clark? Well guess what? She didn't do much of anything. Not really anyways!! Jojo Moyes really should have stopped at <i>Me Before You</i>. But... Yes, I will be moving on to <i>Still Me #3</i> seeing as how it looks like it's much better than this one was :D Fingers Crossed <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1524792214i/25440068._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>“Our eyes locked. And in that moment everything shifted. I saw what I had really done. I saw that I could be somebody’s center, his reason for staying. I saw that I could be enough.”</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524792214ra/25440069.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>“With that kiss, I tried to tell him the enormity of what he meant to me. I tried to show him that he was the answer to a question I hadn’t even known I had been asking. I tried to thank him for wanting me to be me, more than he wanted to make me stay.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9019432324017319775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1476332860" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1166663-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1277905205p2/1166663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1476332860?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/1166663-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780698411418" href="/book/show/25020381-after-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166663-carol?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1476332860" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11184562738935562460">Jo Jo Moyes fans clamored for a sequel to her popular tearjerker <u>Me Before You</u>. I could have left well enough alone but once Moyes jumped on the bandwagon I thought “What the heck?” Many of the reviewers have been disappointed in the way Moyes chose to continue Lou’s story after Will’s death. “Be careful what you wish for.” <br/><br/>I loved and raved about <u>Me Before You </u>. What made that book for me was its relationship to a story from my own life. <br/><br/>If I had read <u>After You</u> as a standalone I might rate it 5</span>
  <span id="freeText11184562738935562460" style="display:none">Jo Jo Moyes fans clamored for a sequel to her popular tearjerker <u>Me Before You</u>. I could have left well enough alone but once Moyes jumped on the bandwagon I thought “What the heck?” Many of the reviewers have been disappointed in the way Moyes chose to continue Lou’s story after Will’s death. “Be careful what you wish for.” <br /><br />I loved and raved about <u>Me Before You </u>. What made that book for me was its relationship to a story from my own life. <br /><br />If I had read <u>After You</u> as a standalone I might rate it 5 stars. As nothing could as good as <u>Me Before You</u>, I’m giving it 4 stars. Perhaps listening was a better choice than reading as Anna Acton, the narrator, brings Lou to life allowing me to experience some of the same things that I loved about the prequel. She does this book proud and it is a smooth, easy listen. The grief, the questioning of life choices, the need to move on, the love story, Lo’s relationships, the humor, all come through loud and clear. I laughed right out loud many times as I walked with those earphones in my ears. <br /><br />I will admit that in the very beginning something happened that had me thinking “Oh no, if that is where this story is going, I’m out” but Moyes managed to move on and I kept walking. <br /><br />One of my GR friends rates Moyes’ books as chick lit, normally not my cup of tea. I prefer to see them as women’s stories, perhaps a tad light, but exploring our feelings just the same. Moyes has become one of my favorite authors. I just like how she writes and sees the world. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11184562738935562460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Maida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5808311-maida"><img alt="Maida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401945746p2/5808311.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1213488967?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maida" href="/user/show/5808311-maida">Maida</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1213488967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4726860480386858386">I finished this novel last night... and I can't even... I can't even bring myself to write a review yet. I am HORRIFIED by what I've just read. <br/><br/>Just so I'm clear: I was NOT opposed to Jojo Moyes writing a sequel to <i>Me Before You.</i> As one of my GR friends so astutely pointed out, the sequel should have been "about Louisa's life afterwards, not constant harping on about Will's past." If it had been done right, the author could have written a beautiful & inspirational novel about Louisa's journey mo</span>
  <span id="freeText4726860480386858386" style="display:none">I finished this novel last night... and I can't even... I can't even bring myself to write a review yet. I am HORRIFIED by what I've just read. <br /><br />Just so I'm clear: I was NOT opposed to Jojo Moyes writing a sequel to <i>Me Before You.</i> As one of my GR friends so astutely pointed out, the sequel should have been "about Louisa's life afterwards, not constant harping on about Will's past." If it had been done right, the author could have written a beautiful &amp; inspirational novel about Louisa's journey moving forward, while still honoring Will's memory. Unfortunately, the novel, instead, dredged up characters from Will's past &amp; added an AWFUL plot twist which was completely uneccessary &amp; which cheapened the storyline, IMO.<br /><br />*** In the end, I would say that approximately 70-75% of this novel is about Will &amp; "other" characters connected to Will's past &amp; only approximately 25-30% about Louisa... thereby relegating Louisa's sense of self-worth, her needs &amp; her desires to "SECOND-PLACE" AGAIN!!! Will's family, nearly everyone associated with Will (and heck, even Louisa's own family) have always and WILL ALWAYS place Louisa's needs &amp; desires LAST. Even the author places Louisa LAST. In this novel, Louisa's personal journey took a backseat to the despicable "plot-twist" &amp; to everything Will-related. It was simply appalling. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>Proper review to come... </b>
</i><br /><b>*1.75/5 stars*</b><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><i>Status Update:</i> March, 2015 ==&gt;&gt; OMG, I need this book NOW. Most highly anticipated release of 2015 for sure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4726860480386858386" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cUnsxcpCgYI1ZWafPhvBcd4GsAVpVCb4uGde078U/hFyRyFYkwPYeN21iF0ixks6ZG7PKqPg+Csnov2paHmVng==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ifOdzlExUfrl8vkBa/bc5PNn3PiSgZviQHq7cWUtuu2K/VBTCHAIAA0iF8N3K1avSQ+j11g1RTHfvxgLskDRYg==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer2622622271206107275">Jojo Moyes is a British novelist.<br/><br/>Moyes studied at Royal Holloway, University of London. She won a bursary financed by The Independent newspaper to study journalism at City University and subsequently worked for <i>The Independent</i> for 10 years. In 2001 she became a full time novelist. <br/><br/>Moyes' novel <i>Foreign Fruit</i> won the Romantic Novelists' Association (RNA) Romantic Novel of the Year in 2004.<br/><br/>She is mar</span>
  <span id="freeText2622622271206107275" style="display:none">Jojo Moyes is a British novelist.<br /><br />Moyes studied at Royal Holloway, University of London. She won a bursary financed by The Independent newspaper to study journalism at City University and subsequently worked for <i>The Independent</i> for 10 years. In 2001 she became a full time novelist. <br /><br />Moyes' novel <i>Foreign Fruit</i> won the Romantic Novelists' Association (RNA) Romantic Novel of the Year in 2004.<br /><br />She is married to journalist Charles Arthur and has three children.</span>

She takes a badly needed job working for ex–Master of the Universe Will Traynor, who is wheelchair bound after an accident. Will has always lived a huge life—big deals, extreme sports, worldwide travel—and now he’s pretty sure he cannot live the way he is.\n\nWill is acerbic, moody, bossy—but Lou refuses to treat him with kid gloves, and soon his happiness means more to her than she expected. When she learns that Will has shocking plans of his own, she sets out to show him that life is still worth living.\n\nA Love Story for this generation and perfect for fans of John Green’s The Fault in Our Stars, Me Before You brings to life two people who couldn’t have less in common—a heartbreakingly romantic novel that asks, What do you do when making the person you love happy also means breaking
